Executor's Rejection and Implied Acceptance by Action
Ruling that rejection in presence is valid; silence with subsequent sale implies acceptance

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings on an executor's rejection in the testator's presence and implied acceptance by action after death, and explain the rational proof based on the testator's lack of authority to compel.

Core Idea
Rejection in presence is valid; silence leaves option; selling estate implies binding acceptance.

In this passage from Al-Hidayah, two crucial scenarios of executorship are clarified. Since the testator cannot compel acceptance, an express rejection in his presence is immediately valid. However, if the executor is silent and then acts by selling estate property after the testator's death, that act constitutes clear evidence of acceptance, making the role binding. Underlying both rulings is the principle that the testator lacks wilayat al-ilzam (authority to compel).

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
The passage presents two distinct cases: (1) explicit rejection during the testator's lifetime in his presence; (2) silence during the testator's lifetime followed by an act of tasarruf (e.g., selling) after death.
The first scenario ends with the testator still alive; the second begins after his death.
2
State the ruling for each scenario
For the first: rejection is valid (sahih) and the executor is freed. For the second: if the executor remains silent, he retains the option after death; but if he sells something, the executorship becomes binding (lazim).
The ruling for silence alone is that he may choose to accept or decline later.
3
Identify the proof (wajh al-dalalah) for each
For rejection: the testator cannot compel (la wilayat al-ilzam), and there is no deception (ghurur) because the testator can appoint another. For implied acceptance: selling is evidence (dalalah) of commitment and acceptance; acceptance after death is valid.
The proof is rational (aqli) based on the nature of the appointment.
4
Understand the underlying principle
The testator's lack of authority to compel (wilayat al-ilzam) means the executor is never forced to accept. Therefore, express rejection is effective immediately, and silence leaves freedom. But once the executor acts in a manner consistent with executorship, he voluntarily commits himself.
This principle distinguishes Hanafi fiqh from systems where a court can compel acceptance.
5
Apply to a novel scenario
Consider: Testator appoints Fatima as executor; Fatima says nothing. After death, she pays an estate debt from her own money. According to the same logic, paying a debt is an act of management that indicates acceptance, so she becomes bound.
Any tasarruf (administrative or disposal) that only an executor would do implies acceptance.

Source Text

فان ردها فى وجهه فهو رد لانه ليس للموصى ولاية الزامه التصرف ولا غرور فيه لانه يمكنه ان ينيب غيره وان لم يقبل ولم يرد حتى مات الموصى فهو بالخيار ان شاء قبل وان شاء لم يقبل لان الموصى ليس له ولاية الالزام فبقى مخيراً فلوانه باع شيئا من تركته فقد لزمته لان ذالك دلالة الالتزام والقبول وهو معتبر بعد الموت

ترجمہ پس اگر وہی نے وصایت کو موصی کے سامنے رد کر دیا تو رد ہو گیا اس لئے کہ موصی کے وصی پر تصرف کو لازم کرنے کی ولایت نہیں ہے اور نہ اس میں کوئی دھوکہ ہے اس لئے کہ موصی کے لئے یہ ممکن ہے کہ وہ اس کے غیر کو نائب بنائے اور اگر وھی نے نہ قبول کیا اور نہ رد کیا یہاں تک کہ موصی مرگیا تو وصی کو اختیار ہے اگر چاہے قبول کرے اور اگر چاہے تو قبول نہ کرے اس لئے کہ موصی کو الزام کی ولا نہیں ہے تو وصی اختیار باقی رہا پس اگر وسی نے موصی کے ترکہ میں سے کوئی چیز بیچ دی تو وصایت اس پر لازم ہوگئی ہے اس لئے کہ یہ ( بیچنا ) التزام اور قبول کرنے کی دلیل ہے اور قبول کرنا موت کے بعد معتبر ہے۔

تشریح اگر خالد نے زید کے سامنے ہی وصایت کو رد کر دیا تو رد ہو جائے گا کیونکہ زید کو یہ اختیار نہیں ہے کہ وہ دوسرے پر اس تصرف کو لازم کر دے یعنی زید کو خالد پر ولایت الزام حاصل نہیں ہے۔ اور جب خالد نے زید کے سامنے رد کیا ہے تو اس میں دھوکہ کی بھی کوئی بات نہیں ہے کیونکہ یہاں زید کسی دوسرے کو اپنا اسی مقرر کر سکتا ہے۔ لمتا اور اگر خالد نے موصی کے کہنے کے بعد نہ قبول کیا اور نہ رد گیا بلکہ خاموش رہا یہاں تک کہ زید کا انتقال ہو گیا تو خالد کو اختیار ہے خواہ قبول کرے خواہ رد کرے اس لئے کہ موصی کو اس پر ولایت الزام حاصل نہیں ہے لہذا خالد کو اختیار ہے ہاں اگر اس نے قبول تو نہیں کیا تھا لیکن زید کے مرنے کے بعد اس کے ترکہ میں سے کسی چیز کو بیچد یا تو اب یہ وصی بن گیا اور ولایت اس کے لئے لازم ہو گئی اس لئے کہ نیہ
If he rejects it in his presence, it is a valid rejection, because the testator does not have the authority to compel him to act, and there is no deception, because he can appoint someone else. And if he neither accepts nor rejects until the testator dies, then he has the option: if he wishes he may accept, and if he wishes he may not accept, because the testator has no authority to compel, so he remains with the option. If he sells something from the estate, then it becomes binding upon him, because that is evidence of commitment and acceptance, and acceptance after death is valid. Commentary: If Khalid rejects the executorship in Zaid's presence, it is valid, because Zaid does not have the authority to compel Khalid to act. There is no deception because Zaid can appoint someone else. And if Khalid neither accepted nor rejected but remained silent until Zaid died, he has the option to accept or reject. However, if after Zaid's death he sells something from the estate, he becomes the executor and the authority becomes binding upon him, because...
Source pages p. 236

Commentary
This passage presents two further rulings on the executor's acceptance and rejection. First, if the executor rejects the appointment in the testator's presence, it is valid. The reason is that the testator cannot compel the executor to accept; there is no element of deception here because the testator is alive and can appoint another. Second, if the executor remains silent and does not accept or reject during the testator's lifetime, and the testator dies, the executor has a choice after death: he may accept or decline. But if he performs any act indicative of acceptance, such as selling an item from the estate, that act constitutes implied acceptance (dalalat al-iltizam wa al-qubul), and the executorship becomes binding on him. This acceptance after death is considered valid. The passage thus balances the testator's lack of compulsion power with the executor's freedom, but once the executor acts, he is bound to continue.

Key Terms
رد (radd): Rejection or revocation of an executorship.
ولایت الزام (wilayat al-ilzam): The authority to compel someone to act.
التزام (iltizam): Commitment or undertaking; acceptance of a duty.
دلالة (dalalah): Evidence or indication; here, selling is evidence of acceptance.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If an executor remains silent during the testator's life and dies, and after the testator's death he sells an item from the estate, what is the ruling?
A) He is not bound to continue as executor
B) He becomes bound as executor because the sale indicates acceptance
C) The sale is invalid because he never formally accepted
D) He must seek court approval to act as executor

Key Takeaway
Rejection in testator's presence is valid and releases the executor; silence leaves an option until death; any act of estate management after death implies binding acceptance.

Wasiyyah — Bequest

Executor's Sale Without Knowledge vs Agent's Sale
Compares validity of sale by executor and agent without knowledge

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the validity of a sale by an executor (wasi) without knowledge, and distinguish it from an agent (wakil) by applying the concepts of khilafah (succession) and inabah (deputyship).

Core Idea
An executor's sale is valid without knowledge; an agent's sale requires knowledge.

This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah explains a key distinction in Hanafi fiqh: the executor (wasi) inherits authority from the deceased like an heir, while the agent (wakil) acts under a living principal. Understanding the difference is crucial for determining the validity of transactions before knowledge of appointment.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Two Scenarios
Pinpoint the two cases: sale by an executor without knowing of his appointment, and sale by an agent without knowing of his agency.
Executor = wasi, Agent = wakil.
2
State the Rulings
Executor's sale is valid and executed (nafidh); agent's sale is not executed (la yanfudh).
The ruling is unconditional for the executor; for the agent, knowledge must exist.
3
Understand the Ratio Legis
Executorship is a form of khilafah (succession) akin to inheritance: no knowledge needed. Agency is inabah (deputyship) which requires the deputy's knowledge.
Khilafah transfers authority from a deceased; inabah delegates from a living person.
4
Apply the Analogy
Just as an heir inherits without knowledge, an executor acts validly. Just as a buyer must know of a purchase to be bound, an agent must know of his appointment.
Qiyas: inheritance → wasaya; purchase → wakala.
5
Note the Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Removal
On the removal (azl) of an agent, Abu Hanifa requires two reporters or one just reporter; Sahibayn accept any single reporter.
This dispute affects how removal is proven, not the main ruling.

Also if he sells something from the testator's estate, is this sale valid or not? And the sale is executed because it issues from the executor, regardless of whether he knew of the executorship or not, unlike the agent if he did not know of the agency and sold, it is not executed. Because executorship is succession; it is specific to the time of cessation of the deceased's authority, so authority transfers to him. And when it is succession, it does not depend on knowledge, like inheritance. As for agency, it is deputyship, established while the principal's authority is ongoing, so it is not valid without his knowledge, like establishing ownership through sale and purchase. And we have already explained the method of knowledge and the condition of notification in previous books. Translation: And the sale will be executed because it issues from the executor, whether he knows of the executorship or not, unlike the agent when he does not know of the agency and sells, it is not executed. Because executorship is succession, because executorship is specific to the time of cessation of the deceased's authority, so authority transfers to him. And when executorship is succession, succession does not depend on knowledge, like the heir. In any case, agency is deputyship, and agency is established while the principal's authority is ongoing, so agency is not valid without the agent's knowledge, like establishing ownership through sale and purchase. And we have explained the method of knowledge and the condition of notification in many previous books. Explanation: The executor sold something from the testator's estate, is this sale valid or not? He said that it is valid and executed, and this sale is also evidence of acceptance. Not only that, even if the executor made the sale and he had not yet known that Zayd appointed him as executor, still the sale is valid and executed. And if Zayd appointed Khalid as agent to sell his goods, and Khalid did not know of the agency, and before knowing he accidentally sold the goods, then the sale is not executed. And the reason for the difference between executorship and agency is that executorship is succession and agency is deputyship. The meaning of succession is that after the testator's death, the executor has authority to dispose. The meaning of deputyship is that the principal is present and has power to dispose, yet he gives authority to the agent, so the agent is the deputy of his principal, not the successor. The two shaykhs are the successors of the Prophet (peace be upon him), and the deputy of the principal is not the successor of the principal, but rather the deputy. When it is known that executorship is succession and agency is deputyship, now hear the separate rules for both. The rule of succession is that it does not need knowledge for its establishment, like inheritance. Since inheritance is succession, whether the heir knows or not, he becomes an heir. Similarly, executorship is succession, so whether the executor knows or not, he becomes executor. And the principle of deputyship is that as long as the deputy does not know that he is the deputy of so-and-so, the deputyship is not established. For example, Zayd bought a horse for Khalid, and Khalid does not know about it, and in that state Khalid disposed of the horse in some way, then the sale is not binding on Khalid because Khalid is not yet aware of the purchase. So Khalid has the option to reject the sale. As for the question of which means of informing the executor or agent is reliable, it has already been covered in many places that knowledge of agency is established by the report of one person, whether that person is free or slave, just or sinful, woman or man, adult or child; this is an agreed ruling. As for the issue of removal (azl), there is a difference between Imam Abu Hanifa and the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad). According to the two companions, removal has the same ruling, i.e., just as knowledge of agency is reliable, the same applies to removal, i.e., it is also established by an absolute report of one person. According to Imam Abu Hanifa, one of two conditions is required: either number (two reporters) or justice, i.e., the reporter of removal must be either two men, or if one, he must be just. The author said that the method of knowledge and condition of notification are not in one place but have been explained in many books of al-Hidayah, i.e., in Kitab Adab al-Qadi, chapter al-Qada' bi al-Mawarith, and in Kitab al-Shuf'ah.
Source pages p. 237

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hidaya is a commentary on al-Hidayah, explaining the ruling regarding a sale conducted by an executor (wasi) or an agent (wakil) without knowledge of their appointment. The passage is a comparative analysis: it first states the ruling, then provides the reasoning using the legal concepts of khilafah (succession) and inabah (deputyship), and finally discusses how knowledge is established, including an intra-Hanafi dispute on the removal (azl) of an agent.

The author confirms that if an executor sells something from the testator's estate before even knowing he was appointed, the sale is valid and executed. This is because executorship (wasaya) is a form of khilafah — the executor steps into the shoes of the deceased after his death, much like an heir inherits without needing to know. In contrast, an agent (wakil) acts under a living principal whose authority continues; thus the agent's authority depends on his knowledge of the agency, just as ownership through purchase requires knowledge of the transaction. The example given is that if Zayd appoints Khalid as agent to sell goods, and Khalid sells them without knowing of the agency, the sale is not valid. Khalid would have the option to reject it, akin to the option of a purchaser who is unaware of a purchase made on his behalf.

Then the text clarifies how knowledge of the agency is established: any single person's report is sufficient, regardless of that person's status (free/slave, just/sinful, male/female, adult/minor). This is an agreed principle. However, regarding the removal (azl) of the agent, there is a dispute: Imam Abu Hanifa requires either two reporters or one just reporter, while the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) accept any single reporter. The author notes that this has been discussed in previous books of al-Hidayah.

Key Terms
وصایة (wasaya): Executorship; a person appointed by a testator to manage his estate after death.
خلافت (khilafah): Succession; the transfer of authority from a deceased person to another, effective immediately after death.
انابت (inabah): Deputyship; an agent acts as deputy for a living principal whose authority continues.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Hanafi fiqh, why is an executor's sale valid without knowledge of his appointment, while an agent's sale is not?
A) Executorship is a form of succession (khilafah), like inheritance, which does not require knowledge.
B) The testator's death terminates all authority, so anyone can act.
C) The executor has a higher level of trust than an agent.
D) Agency requires a written contract; executorship does not.

Key Takeaway
An executor's sale is valid even without knowledge because executorship is succession (khilafah) like inheritance, whereas an agent's sale requires knowledge because agency is deputyship (inabah).

Wasiyyah — Bequest
intermediate
8 min
Acceptance of Executorship After Initial Rejection
Ruling on wasi accepting after rejecting, with dispute with Imam Zufar

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a wasi's acceptance of executorship after initial rejection and identify the condition under which it is valid.

Core Idea
A wasi's rejection does not void the bequest; acceptance remains possible unless the qadi intervenes.

This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah addresses a practical scenario: a person appointed as executor (wasi) initially declines the role after the testator's death, but later changes his mind. The Hanafi school rules that his subsequent acceptance is valid, provided the qadi (judge) has not already removed him. The reasoning balances the harm to the deceased if the bequest is nullified against the harm to the executor, which is compensated by reward. This lesson examines the ruling, its rationale, and the dissenting view of Imam Zufar.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the wasi's acceptance after previously rejecting the executorship. The Hanafi ruling (majority) is that it is valid (sahih) under a condition.
2
Locate the condition
The acceptance is valid only if the qadi has not removed the wasi from the position at the time of rejection or after.
The condition is essential; without it, the acceptance is not valid.
3
Understand the rationale (dalil aqli)
The reasoning uses the principle of repelling greater harm: invalidating the bequest harms the deceased (greater harm), while keeping the wasi harms him but is compensated by reward. So the bequest remains intact.
This is a classic application of the harm principle in Hanafi fiqh.
4
Contrast with Imam Zufar's view
Imam Zufar holds that rejection voids the delegation (tafwīḍ), so acceptance afterwards is impossible. His view gives weight to the wasi's explicit refusal.
Imam Zufar is a Hanafi scholar, but his view is not the muftā bihī position.
5
Recognize the qadi's role
The qadi can remove the wasi as an exercise of ijtihad, because he has authority to prevent harm. If the qadi removes him, the right to accept is lost.
The qadi's decision is effective even if it is based on ijtihad.

If the executor did not accept until the testator died, then he said 'I do not accept' and then said 'I accept', he has that right as long as the qadi has not removed him from the executorship when he said 'I do not accept'. Because merely by saying 'I do not accept' the bequest is not invalidated. Invalidating it harms the deceased, and the harm to the executor in keeping it is compensated by reward. And repelling the first (harm) which is greater is more appropriate. However, if the qadi removes him from executorship, it is valid because it is a matter of ijtihad, and the qadi has authority to repel harm. Translation: And if the executor did not accept until the testator died, then the executor said 'I do not accept' (I do not accept executorship), then said 'I accept', then the executor has the right to do so, provided that the qadi did not remove him from executorship at the time he said 'I do not accept'. Because merely by his saying 'I do not accept', the bequest is not invalidated. Invalidating it harms the deceased, and the harm to the executor in keeping it is compensated by reward. And repelling the first (harm) which is greater is more appropriate. However, when the qadi removes him from executorship, the removal is valid because the qadi's decision is a matter of ijtihad, and the qadi has authority to repel harm. Explanation: When Zayd appointed Khalid as executor, at that time Khalid did not accept. After Zayd's death, he first said 'I do not accept this executorship', then he said 'I have accepted the executorship'. According to us (Hanafis), it is still valid for the executor to accept. Imam Zufar disagrees; he says that after rejection, he no longer has authority to accept because his rejection invalidated the testator's delegation. And when the delegation is invalid, there is no right to accept afterwards. Nevertheless, according to us, he still has the right to accept, but with the condition that the qadi has not removed him from executorship. And if...
Source pages p. 238

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hidaya deals with the situation where a person appointed as executor (wasi) does not accept the appointment before the testator's death, then after death initially rejects it, and later changes his mind and accepts. The text presents the Hanafi ruling along with an intra-Hanafi dispute with Imam Zufar.

The ruling: If the wasi says 'I do not accept' after the testator's death, then later says 'I accept', his acceptance is valid according to the Hanafi school (i.e., Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad al-Shaybani). The reasoning is that the mere statement of rejection does not invalidate the bequest (isā'). Invalidating the bequest would harm the deceased by nullifying his wishes, while keeping the wasi in place only harms the wasi by imposing a responsibility, but this harm is compensated by the reward the wasi receives. Since repelling greater harm (to the deceased) takes priority, the rejection is ineffective unless the qadi explicitly removes him.

Imam Zufar differs: He argues that once the wasi rejects, the delegation (tafwīḍ) from the testator becomes void, so there is no further right to accept. His view gives more weight to the wasi's explicit rejection.

The Hanafi position is conditioned: the acceptance after rejection is only valid if the qadi has not already removed the wasi from the position. If the qadi removes him, it is valid because the qadi's decision is based on ijtihad and he has authority to prevent harm. The text implies that the qadi's removal is effective even if it might not be the only correct view (since it is 'mujtahad fīh').

Key Terms
تفویض (tafwīḍ): Delegation; the testator's appointment of the executor, transferring authority.
ایجاء (īṣā'): Bequest or appointment as executor; the legal act of making a will or appointing a wasi.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school (excluding Imam Zufar), if an executor (wasi) says 'I do not accept' after the testator's death, then later says 'I accept', what condition must be met for his acceptance to be valid?
A) The heirs must approve.
B) The executor must have a valid reason for changing his mind.
C) The qadi must not have removed him from the position.
D) The testator must have specified it in the will.

Key Takeaway
A wasi's initial rejection does not invalidate the bequest; he may still accept unless the qadi has removed him.

Means of Knowledge for Dismissal of a Wasi/Wakil: Difference Between Abu Hanifa and Sahibayn
Clarifies the means of knowledge for appointment and dismissal, highlighting intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions required by Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn for the validity of a dismissal of a wasi/wakil, and identify the practical difference between the two positions.

Core Idea
Appointing a wakil is easy; dismissing him requires more proof according to Abu Hanifa, but not according to the Sahibayn.

In the Hanafi school, the conditions for establishing an agency are lenient: a single report from any person suffices. However, when it comes to dismissing the agent, there is a disagreement between Imam Abu Hanifa and his two disciples, the Sahibayn. This passage explains the different requirements and why this distinction exists.

Guided Path
1
State the agreed rule for appointment
Agency (wakala) is established by a single report from any person, regardless of gender, age, or moral status. This is agreed upon by all Hanafi scholars.
This leniency is based on the principle of facilitating transactions.
2
Identify the point of disagreement
The disagreement concerns dismissal (azl) of an agent or executor. Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn differ on the evidentiary requirement.
The dismissal terminates the authority, which may have serious consequences.
3
Explain Abu Hanifa's position
Abu Hanifa requires either two informants or one just (adil) informant to establish a valid dismissal.
He considers dismissal more serious and thus demands higher reliability.
4
Explain the Sahibayn's position
The Sahibayn hold that a single report from any person suffices for dismissal, just as for appointment.
They see no distinction between creating and terminating authority in terms of evidence.
5
Determine the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
Under Abu Hanifa, a dismissal communicated by a single unjust person is invalid; under the Sahibayn, it is valid. In practice, the Sahibayn's view is preferred for ease.
The mufta bihi (operative position) in later Hanafi practice is the Sahibayn's.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
رہی یہ بات کہ وصی یا وکیل کو آگاہی اور اطلاع کا کون سا ذریعہ معتبر ہے تو وہ ماقبل میں متعدد مقامات پر گذر چکا ہے کہ وکالت کا علم ایک شخص کی خبر سے ثابت ہو جائے گا وہ شخص خواہ آزاد ہو خواہ غلام، عادل ہو یا فاسق ،عورت ہو یا مرد، بالغ ہو یا بچہ یہ تو اتفاقی محکم ہے ، رہا مسئلہ عزل کا تو اس میں امام ابو حنیفہ اور صاحبین کا اختلاف ہے۔ صاحبین کے نزدیک عزل کا بھی یہی حکم ہے یعنی جس طرح وکالت کا علم معتبر ہے اسی طرح عزل کا حکم ہے یعنی مطلق خبر واحد سے اس کا بھی ثبوت ہو جائے گا۔ اور امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک دو چیزوں میں سے ایک شرط ہے یا تو عدد ہو یا عدالت یعنی عزل کی خبر دینے والے یا تو دو آدمی ہوں اور اگر ایک ہو تو اس کا عادل ہونا ضروری ہے۔ اسی کو مصنف نے فرمایا ہے کہ علم کے ذریعہ اور اخبار کی شرط ایک جگہ نہیں بلکہ ہدایہ کی متعدد کتابوں میں بیان کر چکے ہیں یعنی کتاب ادب القاضی کی فصل القضاء بالمواریث میں اور کتاب الشفعہ میں بیان کیا ہے۔
Remaining is this matter: what source of knowledge and information is reliable for the executor or agent? It has passed in multiple previous places that knowledge of agency is established by the report of one person, whether that person is free or slave, just or sinful, woman or man, adult or child — this is an agreed upon ruling. As for the issue of dismissal, there is disagreement between Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn. According to the Sahibayn, the rule for dismissal is the same: just as knowledge of agency is reliable, so is the rule for dismissal, i.e., it is also established by an absolute single report. According to Imam Abu Hanifa, one of two conditions is required: either number or justice — meaning the informant of dismissal must be two people, and if one, then he must be just. The author [Marghinani] stated that the condition of knowledge and report is not uniform; rather it has been explained in multiple books of Hidayah, namely in the chapter of 'Judgment on Inheritances' in Kitab Adab al-Qadi, and in Kitab al-Shuf'ah.
Source pages p. 238

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute. It first establishes a general principle: knowledge of an agency (wakala) is reliably established by a single report from any person, regardless of gender, age, or moral status. This is agreed upon. Then it addresses the specific case of dismissal (azl) of an agent or executor (wasi). Here, Imam Abu Hanifa differs from his two disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani (the Sahibayn). The Sahibayn apply the same lenient rule: a single report suffices. Imam Abu Hanifa demands additional reliability: either two informants or one just informant. The author notes that this distinction is not an inconsistency but is stated in various places in the Hidayah, specifically in Kitab Adab al-Qadi and Kitab al-Shuf'ah. The practical effect is that a wasi dismissed by a single unjust report is not validly dismissed in Abu Hanifa's view.

Key Terms
عزل (‘azl): Dismissal of an agent or executor from his role
خبر واحد (khabar wāhid): A report from a single person, without additional corroboration

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) A single report from any person
B) Either two informants or one just informant
C) A written document from the testator
D) Confirmation by the Qadi

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, dismissal of an executor requires stronger evidence according to Abu Hanifa, but the Sahibayn accept a single report; the later preferred view is the Sahibayn's.

Executor's Acceptance After Rejection: The Qadi's Role
Ruling on executor's rejection then acceptance

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on an executor's acceptance after initial rejection and explain why the Qadi's removal terminates that right.

Core Idea
An executor who initially rejects may later accept, unless the Qadi has already removed him to prevent harm.

This lesson examines the Hanafi position on an executor who first refuses the executorship and later changes his mind. The ruling balances the testator's trust and the need to prevent harm, while recognizing the Qadi's authority to intervene. We will explore the proof based on istihsan and the disagreement with Imam Zufar.

Guided Path
1
State the Scenario and Hanafi Ruling
Identify the sequence: executor named, does not accept initially, testator dies, executor says 'I do not accept' then later 'I accept'. According to the majority (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad), this later acceptance is valid (sahih).
The executor's mere words 'I do not accept' do not invalidate the will.
2
Identify the Proof (Istihsan)
The ruling is based on istihsan: preserving the will to avoid harm (ḍarar) to the deceased outweighs the formal qiyas that rejection nullifies delegation. The executor's burden is compensated by reward.
The principle 'al-ḍarar al-ashadd yuzāl bi al-ḍarar al-akhaff' (the greater harm is removed by enduring the lesser) applies.
3
Note the Condition: Qadi's Non-Intervention
The executor's right to change his mind exists only if the Qadi has not already removed him from executorship at the time of the initial refusal. If the Qadi removed him, the later acceptance is void.
The Qadi's removal is an ijtihadi matter and binding.
4
Understand Imam Zufar's Objection and Hanafi Response
Imam Zufar holds that rejection nullifies the delegation irrevocably, so later acceptance is invalid. The Hanafi majority counters that the testator's interest (reward) and harm prevention take precedence.
The dispute is within the Hanafi school; the mufta bihi is the majority view.
5
Grasp the Qadi's Authority and Its Effect
The Qadi has vilāyah (authority) to remove an executor to prevent harm. Once he does, the executor cannot become executor again because the Qadi's ruling is binding in ijtihadi matters.
This shows the balance between individual rights and judicial authority.

[Ruling:] And if the executor had not accepted until the testator died, then he said 'I do not accept' then said 'I accept', he has that right as long as the Qadi had not removed him from executorship when he said 'I do not accept', because by his mere saying 'I do not accept' the will is not invalidated, for invalidating it involves harm to the deceased, and the harm to the executor in keeping it is compensated by reward, and repelling the first is higher and more appropriate. However, if the Qadi removed him from executorship, that removal is valid because it is a matter of ijtihad, for the Qadi has authority to repel harm.
[Translation:] And if the executor had not accepted until the testator died, then the executor said 'I do not accept' then said 'I accept', then the executor has that right if the Qadi had not removed him from the will when he said 'I do not accept', because by his mere saying 'I do not accept' the will is not invalidated; because invalidating it involves harm to the deceased, and the harm to the executor in keeping it is compensated by reward, and repelling the first is more appropriate. But when the Qadi removed the executor from executorship, this removal is correct because the Qadi's ruling is in matters of ijtihad, for the Qadi has authority to repel harm from people.
[Commentary:] When Zayd appointed Khalid as executor, at that time Khalid did not accept, and after Zayd's death, initially he said 'I do not accept this executorship', then later he said 'I have accepted the executorship'. According to us, the executor's acceptance is still valid. Imam Zufar differs; he says that after rejection, the authority to accept no longer remains, because his rejection invalidated the testator's delegation, and when the delegation is invalidated, there is no right to accept thereafter. Nevertheless, according to us, there is still a right to accept, but the condition is that the Qadi had not removed him from executorship. And if at the time of his saying 'I do not accept', the Qadi had removed him from executorship, then after the Qadi's removal, he no longer has the right to become executor, because when he said 'I do not accept', the will was not invalidated merely by that saying. The reason: if we invalidate the will, there is harm to the deceased, because he departed from this world trusting in him. So to protect the deceased from harm, the will is not invalidated. And keeping the will in effect benefits the deceased, but it harms the executor because executorship becomes binding on him, and he may be unable to fulfill its responsibilities. The answer given is that the harm to the executor is compensated by reward; he will obtain reward in the Hereafter. Or it can be said that these are two harms: the harm to the deceased is primary and superior, the executor's is lesser, and the lesser harm is endured to repel the greater harm. Therefore, the lesser harm is borne. But if the Qadi removed him from executorship, the removal is valid, because the Qadi's ruling is in matters of ijtihad, and when the Qadi's ruling in ijtihadi matters is issued, it becomes binding; thus the will becomes invalid, because the Qadi did this to repel harm, and the Qadi has authority to repel harm from people.
Source pages p. 238

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof, explaining the permissibility of an executor accepting the executorship after first rejecting it, but only if the Qadi had not already removed him. The reasoning is based on preventing harm to the deceased: invalidating the will would harm the testator who relied on that person. The potential harm to the executor (being burdened with duties) is outweighed by the reward he will receive. Imam Zufar holds a stricter view: rejection nullifies the delegation entirely. The Hanafi school (Abu Hanifa and Sahibayn) disagrees, emphasizing the primacy of fulfilling the deceased's trust. The Qadi's authority to remove an executor is recognized because his judgment in ijtihadi matters is binding and he has the power to prevent harm. The practical outcome: an executor who initially refuses may change his mind and accept, unless the Qadi has already acted.

Key Terms
وصایت (wasāyah): The office of executor; the responsibility assigned by a testator to manage his estate after death
قبول (qubūl): Acceptance of the executorship; without it the will is not binding on the executor
ضرر (ḍarar): Harm or detriment, used as a basis for legal rulings (la darar wa la dirar)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The executor must have a valid excuse for the delay.
B) The Qadi must not have removed the executor at the time of rejection.
C) The testator must have died within a year.
D) The executor must accept within three days of the testator's death.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, an executor may validly accept executorship after initially rejecting it, provided the Qadi has not already removed him; the ruling is based on istihsan to prevent harm to the deceased.

Qadi's Authority to Dismiss an Incapacitated Executor
Ruling with proof: Qadi's authority to dismiss executor

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the Qadi's power to remove an executor and apply the principle of repelling harm (raf' al-darar) to justify this intervention.

Core Idea
The Qadi can remove an incapable executor and appoint a guardian to prevent harm to both sides.

We now examine a specific, practical authority of the Qadi in estate management. The Hanafi school holds that when an executor becomes incapable of performing his duties, the Qadi may dismiss him and appoint a guardian to protect the testator's estate. This lesson explores the ruling, its justification based on the principle of repelling harm, and the binding effect of the Qadi's decision.

Guided Path
1
Identify the issue and the premise
The text asks whether the Qadi can dismiss an executor. The premise is that the executor may be unable to perform his duties, causing him harm if the executorship continues.
Harm (darar) here refers to the executor's personal difficulty or inability to manage the estate obligations.
2
Understand the Qadi's action
The Qadi repels harm by removing the executor and appointing a guardian (hafiz) to manage the deceased's property. This action is effective and binding.
The guardian acts only to preserve and administer the estate, not as an executor.
3
Note the consequence of removal
After the Qadi removes the executor, even if the executor later says 'I accept', his acceptance is ignored because the executorship has been annulled by the Qadi.
The Qadi's annulment is final — the executor loses the right to accept.
4
Trace the proof
The ruling is based on istihsan (juristic preference) using the principle of repelling harm (raf' al-darar). The Qadi has general wilayah to prevent harm, so he can remove the executor and appoint a guardian.
This is a dalil aqli (rational proof) — necessity and public interest justify the intervention.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قاضی کو وصی کی وصایت سے معزول کرنے کا حق حاصل ہے یا نہیں و ربما يعجز عن ذالك فيتضرر ببقاء الوصاية فيدفع القاضى الضرر عنه و ينصب حافظاً لمال الميت متصرفا فيه فيندفع الضرر من الجانبين فلهذا ينفذ اخراجه فلو قال بعد اخراج القاضى اياه اقبل لم يلتفت اليه لانه قبل بعد بطلان الوصاية بابطال القاضى ترجمہ اور بسا اوقات وہی اس سے ( وصایت کے فرائض انجام دینے سے عاجز ہوتا ہے تو وصی ضرر محسوس کرے گا وصایت کے باقی رہنے سے تو قاضی ہی سے ضرر کو دور کرے گا اور میت کے مال کے لئے کوئی نگراں مقرر کرے گا جو میت کے مال میں تصرف کرے گا تو جائین کا ضرر دور ہو جائے گا اس وجہ سے قاضی کا اخراج نافذ ہوگا پس اگر وصی نے قاضی کے اس کو خارج کرنے کے بعد اقبل کہا تو اس کی جانب التفات نہیں کیا جائے گا اس لئے کہ وصی نے وصایت کے بطلان کے بعد قبول کیا ہے جو قاضی کے ابطال سے باطل ہوتی ہے۔ تشریح وہی پہلی بات باقی ہے کہ قاضی کو یہ ولایت ہے کہ وصی کو وصایت سے خارج کر دے کیونکہ ہو سکتا ہے کہ وصی وصایت کے فرائض انجام دینے سے عاجز ہو اور اس کے باوجود بھی وصایت کو باقی رکھا جائے تو اس میں وصی کا ضرر ہے لہذا قاضی کو حق ہوگا کہ وہ جی کو وصایت سے خارج قرار دے کر وصی کے ضرر کو دور کرے اور میت کے مال کے لئے کوئی نگراں مقرر کر دے جو مال میت نہیں تصرف کرے تو اس تدبیر سے جانین کا ضرر دور ہو جائے گا لہذا قاضی نے جو وصی کو وصایت سے خارج کیا تو اس کا
[Heading:] Does the Qadi have the right to dismiss the executor from executorship or not? [Arabic:] And perhaps he (the executor) is unable to do that (the duties), so he is harmed by the continuation of executorship; then the Qadi repels the harm from him and appoints a guardian over the deceased's property who acts in it, so the harm is repelled from both sides. For this reason, his (the Qadi's) removal is effective. If after the Qadi's removal of him, he says 'I accept', no attention is paid to him, because he accepted after the invalidation of the executorship by the Qadi's annulment. [Translation:] And sometimes the executor is unable to perform the duties of executorship, so he feels harm from the continuation of executorship; then the Qadi repels the harm from him and appoints a guardian for the deceased's property who will dispose of the deceased's property; thus the harm from both sides is repelled. For this reason, the Qadi's removal is effective. So if the executor, after the Qadi removed him, says 'I accept', it will not be paid attention to, because the executor accepted after the annulment of executorship, which is invalidated by the Qadi's annulment. [Commentary:] The same previous point remains: the Qadi has this authority to dismiss the executor from executorship, because it is possible that the executor is unable to perform the duties of executorship, and if despite that executorship is kept in place, there is harm to the executor. Therefore, the Qadi will have the right to remove the executor from executorship to repel the executor's harm, and appoint a guardian for the deceased's property who will dispose of the deceased's property? Then by this measure, harm from both sides will be repelled. Therefore, when the Qadi removed the executor from executorship, then his (the text ends).
Source pages p. 239

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof, specifically addressing the Qadi's authority to remove an executor. The key principle is the prevention of harm: if the executor is unable to perform his duties, continuing the executorship causes him harm. The Qadi can remove him and appoint a guardian (hafiz) to manage the estate, thus preventing harm to both the executor and the deceased's beneficiaries. The Qadi's decision is binding because it is an ijtihadi matter. Once removed, the executor cannot later accept the executorship, as it has been annulled. This complements the previous lesson: the Qadi's intervention overrides the executor's right to accept after refusal.

Key Terms
اخراج (ikhrāj): Removal of the executor by the Qadi from his position
ولایت (wilāyah): Authority or jurisdiction of the Qadi to take necessary actions, including dismissing executors

Key Takeaway
When an executor becomes incapable, the Qadi may dismiss him and appoint a guardian to protect the estate; the removal annuls the executorship permanently.

Qadi's Authority to Remove a Wasi and the Legal Effect of Refusal
Qadi's removal authority and effect of wasi's refusal

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a wasi's refusal and explain the qadi's authority to remove a wasi to prevent harm.

Core Idea
A wasi's refusal does not invalidate the wasiyyah; the qadi may remove a wasi to prevent harm, and after removal the wasi cannot later accept.

This lesson addresses two key questions in Hanafi wasiyyah law: first, what happens when a person appointed as wasi immediately refuses the appointment? Second, under what conditions can the qadi remove a wasi? The passage explains that the deceased's interest is prioritized over the wasi's burden, and the qadi has the authority to remove a wasi who is unable to perform the duties.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling on a wasi's refusal
The text states that if the appointed wasi says 'I do not accept', the wasiyyah is not invalidated. This ruling protects the deceased's reliance and interest. The wasi's potential harm is mitigated by the promise of reward in the Hereafter.
The key principle: the deceased's harm (greater) is prevented by enduring the wasi's lesser harm.
2
Understand the qadi's removal authority
The qadi has the authority to remove a wasi if the wasi is unable to perform his duties and suffers harm. The qadi then appoints a guardian for the estate, removing harm from both sides.
The qadi's decision is in ijtihad matters and thus binding.
3
Determine the effect of removal
After the qadi's removal, the wasi cannot later accept the wasiyyah, because the qadi's nullification has rendered the appointment invalid.
This is because the wasiyyah is void from the moment of qadi's removal.

Source Text

كتاب الوصايا
اور اگر روسی اخراج قاضی کے بعد کہتا ہے کہ میں قبول کرتا ہوں تو اس کے قبول کی جانب التفات نہ ہو گا اس لئے کہ اب قبول بعد کرنے سے کوئی فائدہ نہیں جب کہ قاضی کے ابطال کی وجہ سے وصایت باطل ہو چکی ہے۔
قاضی کسی کے وصی غلام ، کافر اور فاسق کو وصایت سے نکال سکتا ہے
قال ومن اوصى الى عبد او كافر او فاسق اخرجهم القاضى عن الوصاية و نصب غيرهم وهذا اللفظ يشير الى صحة الوصية لان الاخراج يكون بعدها و ذكر محمد فى الاصل ان الوصية باطلة قيل معناه في جميع هذه الصوران الوصية ستبطل وقيل فى العبد معناه باطل حقيقة لعدم ولايته واستبداده و في معناه غيره ستبطل و قيل فى الكافر باطل ايضا لعدم ولايته على المسلم
ترجمہ قدوری نے فرمایا اور جس نے کسی غلام یا کافر یا فاسق کو بھی بنایا تو قاضی ان کو وصایت سے خارج کر دے گا اور ان کے غیر کو مقرر کرے گا اور قدوری کا یہ لفظ وصیت کی صحت کی جانب مشیر ہے اس لئے کہ اخراج صحت کے بعد ہوتا ہے اور محمد نے مبسوط میں ذکر کیا ہے کہ وصیت باطل ہے کہا گیا ہے کہ اس کے معنی ان تمام صورتوں میں یہ ہیں کہ وصیت عنقریب باطل کر دی جائے گی اور کہا گیا ہے کہ غلام کے سلسلہ میں اس کے معنی حقیقتہ باطل ہونے کے ہیں غلام کی عدم ولایت اور عدم استقلال کی وجہ سے اور غلام کے غیر میں اس کے معنی ستبطل کے ہیں اور کہا گیا ہے کہ کافر میں بھی باطل ہے کافر کی مسلمان پر ولایت نہ ہونے کی وجہ سے۔ تشریح اگر زید نے خالد کے غلام کو اپنا وصی بنا یا کسی کا فر یا فاسق کو اپنا وصی بنایا تو امام قدوری نے کہا ہے کہ قاضی ان تینوں کو وصایت سے خارج کر دے گا اور ان کے علاوہ کو مقرر کر دے گا ، اب اس پر صاحب ہدایہ کچھ تبصرہ فرما رہے ہیں کہ امام قدوری کا یہ کلام اس بات کو واضح کرتا ہے کہ وصیت صحیح ہو جائے گی اس لئے کہ اخراج اس وقت ہوگا جب کہ وصیت صحیح ہوگئی ہو۔
اور امام محمد نے مبسوط میں یہ فرمایا ہے کہ وصیت باطل ہے اب اس کی تشریح میں اقوال مختلفہ ہیں۔ - فقیہ ابواللیث نے جامع صغیر کی شرح میں امام محمد کے اس قول مذکور کے یہ معنی بیان کئے ہیں کہ وصیت ان تینوں صورتوں میں اس قابل ہے کہ اس کو باطل قرار دیا جائے تو چونکہ یہ وصیت باطل کئے جانے کے قابل ہے اس لئے اس کو پہلے ہی سے باطل کہ دیا
گیا ہے۔ اور بعض حضرات نے کہا ہے کہ غلام کی صورت میں تو یہ بطلان اپنی حقیقت پر محمول ہے یعنی وصیت سرے ہی سے باطل ہے کیونکہ
غلام کے اندر یہ ولایت نہیں ہے اور نہ غلام کو استقلال حاصل ہے کیونکہ وہ اپنے مولیٰ کے قبضہ اور اس کے اختیار میں ہے۔ -۳- اور بعض حضرات نے کہا ہے کہ اگر کا فرکو ھی بنایا گیا تو یہ بھی سرے ہی سے باطل ہے کیونکہ کا فر بھی مسلمان پر ولایت نہیں رکھتا اور نہ اس میں یہ اہلیت ہے کہ وہ مسلمان کا ولی بن سکے ۔ "
وصیت کی صحت ، قاضی کے اخراج کی صحت کی وجہ
ووجه الصحة ثم الاخراج ان اسل النظر ثابت لقدرة العبد حقيقة وولاية الفاسق على اصلنا وولاية الكافر
Book of Wasiyyah. Ashraf al-Bidaya, Urdu commentary of Bidaya, Volume 16. If when he said 'I do not accept' the qadi had removed him from the wasiyyah, then after the qadi's removal he no longer has the right to become wasi, because when he said 'I do not accept', the wasiyyah was not invalidated merely by that saying. The reason is that if we invalidate the wasiyyah, there is harm to the deceased, because he departed the world relying on it. So to protect the deceased from harm, the wasiyyah is not invalidated. And keeping the wasiyyah in place benefits the deceased, but it harms the wasi because the responsibility of wasiyyah becomes obligatory upon him and he may be unable to fulfill it. The response is that the wasi also has harm, but his harm is compensated by reward in the Hereafter. Or it can be said that both are harms, but the deceased's harm is greater and higher, while the wasi's harm is lesser, and the lesser harm is endured to remove the greater harm. However, if the qadi has removed him from the wasiyyah, the qadi's removal is valid because this ruling is in matters of ijtihad, and when the qadi gives a ruling in ijtihad matters, it becomes binding. Thus the wasiyyah becomes invalid because the qadi did this to remove harm, and the qadi has authority to remove harm from people. Does the qadi have the right to remove the wasi from his wasiyyah or not? 'And perhaps he may be unable to do so and be harmed by the continuation of the wasiyyah, so the qadi removes the harm from him and appoints a guardian for the deceased's wealth who may dispose of it, so harm is removed from both sides. Therefore his removal is effective. If after the qadi's removal he says 'I accept', it is not heeded, because he accepted after the wasiyyah was rendered invalid by the qadi's nullification.' Translation: Sometimes the wasi is unable to perform the duties and is harmed by the continuation of the wasiyyah. So the qadi will remove the harm from him and appoint a supervisor for the deceased's property who will manage it, so harm from both sides is removed. For this reason, the qadi's removal is effective. If after the qadi's removal the wasi says 'I accept', it will not be heeded because he accepted after the wasiyyah became invalid due to the qadi's nullification. Commentary: The first point remains: the qadi has authority to remove the wasi because the wasi may be unable to perform the duties of the wasiyyah, and if the wasiyyah is kept in place, there is harm to the wasi. So the qadi has the right to remove him and appoint a guardian for the deceased's property to manage it, thus removing harm from both sides. Therefore the qadi's removal is effective. And if after the qadi's removal the wasi says 'I accept', it will not be heeded because now there is no benefit in accepting after the wasiyyah has been invalidated by the qadi. The qadi can remove a wasi who is a slave, kafir, or fasiq. He said: 'Whoever appoints a slave, a kafir, or a fasiq as wasi, the qadi removes them from the wasiyyah and appoints others.' This wording indicates the validity of the wasiyyah because removal occurs after its validity. Muhammad mentioned in al-Asl that the wasiyyah is invalid. It is said: its meaning in all these cases is that the wasiyyah will become invalid. It is said: in the case of a slave, it is actually invalid due to his lack of authority and independence. In other cases it will become invalid. It is said: in the case of a kafir, it is also invalid due to his lack of authority over a Muslim. Translation: Quduri said: Whoever appoints a slave, a kafir, or a fasiq as wasi, the qadi will remove them from the wasiyyah and appoint others. Quduri's wording indicates the validity of the wasiyyah because removal occurs after validity. Muhammad mentioned in al-Mabsut that the wasiyyah is invalid. There are different interpretations. Faqih Abu al-Layth in his commentary on al-Jami' al-Saghir interpreted Muhammad's statement to mean that the wasiyyah is susceptible to being invalidated, so it is declared invalid from the start. Some said: in the case of a slave, this invalidity is literal, i.e., the wasiyyah is invalid from the beginning because the slave has no authority or independence. Some said: if a kafir is appointed, it is also invalid from the beginning because a kafir has no authority over a Muslim. The validity of the wasiyyah and the validity of the qadi's removal: 'And the basis of validity is that the capacity for supervision (al-nazar) is established for the ability of the slave in reality, and for the authority of the fasiq according to our principle, and for the authority of the kafir.'
Source pages p. 239

Commentary
This passage addresses two interrelated issues: the qadi's authority to remove a wasi (executor) and the validity of a wasiyyah when the appointed wasi is a slave, a kafir, or a fasiq. The commentator begins by explaining that if a person appointed as wasi initially refuses (by saying 'I do not accept'), the wasiyyah does not become invalid simply because of that refusal. The reason is to protect the interest of the deceased, who relied on that person. The wasi's refusal causes harm to the deceased if the wasiyyah is invalidated. However, the wasi may also suffer harm if forced to serve, but this is mitigated by the promise of reward in the Hereafter. The qadi has the authority to remove a wasi to prevent harm, and such removal is effective. After removal, the wasi cannot later accept because the wasiyyah has been nullified by the qadi's ruling. The second part discusses the case where the deceased appoints a slave, a kafir, or a fasiq as wasi. According to Quduri, the wasiyyah is valid, and the qadi may remove them and appoint someone else. Imam Muhammad holds that the wasiyyah is invalid. The commentator reconciles these views: some say it means the wasiyyah will eventually be invalidated; others say it is invalid from the start for a slave due to lack of capacity, and for a kafir due to lack of authority over a Muslim. The preferred view (as indicated by the text) is that the wasiyyah is valid, and the qadi's removal is based on his supervisory authority to ensure proper management of the deceased's estate.

Key Terms
وصی (wasi): The person appointed by the testator to execute the will and manage the estate after death.
وصایت (wisayah): The office or responsibility of being a wasi; the executorship of a will.
قاضی (qadi): The Islamic judge who has authority (wilayah) to remove a wasi if necessary to prevent harm.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the effect of the qadi's removal of a wasi?
A) The wasi can still accept the wasiyyah later.
B) The wasiyyah becomes invalid and the wasi cannot later accept.
C) The wasi must appeal the removal to a higher court.
D) The removal is only temporary pending the wasi's performance.

Key Takeaway
A wasi's refusal does not invalidate the wasiyyah; the qadi may remove a wasi to prevent harm, and after removal the wasi cannot later accept.

Wasiyyah — Bequest
intermediate
8 min
Validity of Wasiyyah to a Slave, Kafir, or Fasiq: The Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on validity of wasiyyah to a slave, kafir, or fasiq

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two Hanafi positions on the validity of a wasiyyah to a slave, kafir, or fasiq, and explain the preferred view with its evidence.

Core Idea
Quduri implies the wasiyyah is valid, while Imam Muhammad says it is invalid; the preferred view is validity with qadi's removal.

This lesson examines a classic intra-Hanafi dispute: when a testator appoints a slave, a non-Muslim (kafir), or a corrupt person (fasiq) as executor, is the appointment valid? Imam Quduri's text suggests validity, while Imam Muhammad explicitly states invalidity. The commentator reconciles these views, and the preferred position is that the wasiyyah is valid, but the qadi may remove such a wasi to ensure proper management of the estate.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two positions
Quduri's wording: 'Whoever appoints a slave, a kafir, or a fasiq as wasi, the qadi removes them and appoints others' suggests the wasiyyah is valid because removal occurs after validity. Imam Muhammad in al-Asl states the wasiyyah is invalid.
The phrase 'this wording indicates the validity of the wasiyyah' is key.
2
Examine Imam Muhammad's statement and its interpretations
Imam Muhammad's statement is interpreted in three ways: (1) the wasiyyah will become invalid eventually, (2) for a slave it is actually invalid due to lack of capacity, (3) for a kafir it is also invalid due to lack of authority over a Muslim.
These interpretations aim to reconcile Quduri and Muhammad.
3
Understand the basis for validity
The text states that the capacity for supervision (al-nazar) is established for the slave in reality, for the fasiq according to Hanafi principles, and for the kafir (though limited). Thus the appointment can be valid, but the qadi may remove them to prevent harm.
This is the talil (legal reasoning) supporting validity.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf and tarjih
If the wasiyyah is invalid, no appointment is made; the qadi must appoint an administrator. If valid, the wasi's appointment stands until removal. The preferred view (mufta bihi) is validity, as indicated by Quduri's wording and the qadi's removal being conditional on a valid wasiyyah.
Tarjih authority: The commentator of Hidayah favors Quduri's implication.

كتاب الوصايا
اور اگر روسی اخراج قاضی کے بعد کہتا ہے کہ میں قبول کرتا ہوں تو اس کے قبول کی جانب التفات نہ ہو گا اس لئے کہ اب قبول بعد کرنے سے کوئی فائدہ نہیں جب کہ قاضی کے ابطال کی وجہ سے وصایت باطل ہو چکی ہے۔
قاضی کسی کے وصی غلام ، کافر اور فاسق کو وصایت سے نکال سکتا ہے
قال ومن اوصى الى عبد او كافر او فاسق اخرجهم القاضى عن الوصاية و نصب غيرهم وهذا اللفظ يشير الى صحة الوصية لان الاخراج يكون بعدها و ذكر محمد فى الاصل ان الوصية باطلة قيل معناه في جميع هذه الصوران الوصية ستبطل وقيل فى العبد معناه باطل حقيقة لعدم ولايته واستبداده و في معناه غيره ستبطل و قيل فى الكافر باطل ايضا لعدم ولايته على المسلم
ترجمہ قدوری نے فرمایا اور جس نے کسی غلام یا کافر یا فاسق کو بھی بنایا تو قاضی ان کو وصایت سے خارج کر دے گا اور ان کے غیر کو مقرر کرے گا اور قدوری کا یہ لفظ وصیت کی صحت کی جانب مشیر ہے اس لئے کہ اخراج صحت کے بعد ہوتا ہے اور محمد نے مبسوط میں ذکر کیا ہے کہ وصیت باطل ہے کہا گیا ہے کہ اس کے معنی ان تمام صورتوں میں یہ ہیں کہ وصیت عنقریب باطل کر دی جائے گی اور کہا گیا ہے کہ غلام کے سلسلہ میں اس کے معنی حقیقتہ باطل ہونے کے ہیں غلام کی عدم ولایت اور عدم استقلال کی وجہ سے اور غلام کے غیر میں اس کے معنی ستبطل کے ہیں اور کہا گیا ہے کہ کافر میں بھی باطل ہے کافر کی مسلمان پر ولایت نہ ہونے کی وجہ سے۔ تشریح اگر زید نے خالد کے غلام کو اپنا وصی بنا یا کسی کا فر یا فاسق کو اپنا وصی بنایا تو امام قدوری نے کہا ہے کہ قاضی ان تینوں کو وصایت سے خارج کر دے گا اور ان کے علاوہ کو مقرر کر دے گا ، اب اس پر صاحب ہدایہ کچھ تبصرہ فرما رہے ہیں کہ امام قدوری کا یہ کلام اس بات کو واضح کرتا ہے کہ وصیت صحیح ہو جائے گی اس لئے کہ اخراج اس وقت ہوگا جب کہ وصیت صحیح ہوگئی ہو۔
اور امام محمد نے مبسوط میں یہ فرمایا ہے کہ وصیت باطل ہے اب اس کی تشریح میں اقوال مختلفہ ہیں۔ - فقیہ ابواللیث نے جامع صغیر کی شرح میں امام محمد کے اس قول مذکور کے یہ معنی بیان کئے ہیں کہ وصیت ان تینوں صورتوں میں اس قابل ہے کہ اس کو باطل قرار دیا جائے تو چونکہ یہ وصیت باطل کئے جانے کے قابل ہے اس لئے اس کو پہلے ہی سے باطل کہ دیا
گیا ہے۔ اور بعض حضرات نے کہا ہے کہ غلام کی صورت میں تو یہ بطلان اپنی حقیقت پر محمول ہے یعنی وصیت سرے ہی سے باطل ہے کیونکہ
غلام کے اندر یہ ولایت نہیں ہے اور نہ غلام کو استقلال حاصل ہے کیونکہ وہ اپنے مولیٰ کے قبضہ اور اس کے اختیار میں ہے۔ -۳- اور بعض حضرات نے کہا ہے کہ اگر کا فرکو ھی بنایا گیا تو یہ بھی سرے ہی سے باطل ہے کیونکہ کا فر بھی مسلمان پر ولایت نہیں رکھتا اور نہ اس میں یہ اہلیت ہے کہ وہ مسلمان کا ولی بن سکے ۔ "
وصیت کی صحت ، قاضی کے اخراج کی صحت کی وجہ
ووجه الصحة ثم الاخراج ان اسل النظر ثابت لقدرة العبد حقيقة وولاية الفاسق على اصلنا وولاية الكافر
Book of Wasiyyah. Ashraf al-Bidaya, Urdu commentary of Bidaya, Volume 16. If when he said 'I do not accept' the qadi had removed him from the wasiyyah, then after the qadi's removal he no longer has the right to become wasi, because when he said 'I do not accept', the wasiyyah was not invalidated merely by that saying. The reason is that if we invalidate the wasiyyah, there is harm to the deceased, because he departed the world relying on it. So to protect the deceased from harm, the wasiyyah is not invalidated. And keeping the wasiyyah in place benefits the deceased, but it harms the wasi because the responsibility of wasiyyah becomes obligatory upon him and he may be unable to fulfill it. The response is that the wasi also has harm, but his harm is compensated by reward in the Hereafter. Or it can be said that both are harms, but the deceased's harm is greater and higher, while the wasi's harm is lesser, and the lesser harm is endured to remove the greater harm. However, if the qadi has removed him from the wasiyyah, the qadi's removal is valid because this ruling is in matters of ijtihad, and when the qadi gives a ruling in ijtihad matters, it becomes binding. Thus the wasiyyah becomes invalid because the qadi did this to remove harm, and the qadi has authority to remove harm from people. Does the qadi have the right to remove the wasi from his wasiyyah or not? 'And perhaps he may be unable to do so and be harmed by the continuation of the wasiyyah, so the qadi removes the harm from him and appoints a guardian for the deceased's wealth who may dispose of it, so harm is removed from both sides. Therefore his removal is effective. If after the qadi's removal he says 'I accept', it is not heeded, because he accepted after the wasiyyah was rendered invalid by the qadi's nullification.' Translation: Sometimes the wasi is unable to perform the duties and is harmed by the continuation of the wasiyyah. So the qadi will remove the harm from him and appoint a supervisor for the deceased's property who will manage it, so harm from both sides is removed. For this reason, the qadi's removal is effective. If after the qadi's removal the wasi says 'I accept', it will not be heeded because he accepted after the wasiyyah became invalid due to the qadi's nullification. Commentary: The first point remains: the qadi has authority to remove the wasi because the wasi may be unable to perform the duties of the wasiyyah, and if the wasiyyah is kept in place, there is harm to the wasi. So the qadi has the right to remove him and appoint a guardian for the deceased's property to manage it, thus removing harm from both sides. Therefore the qadi's removal is effective. And if after the qadi's removal the wasi says 'I accept', it will not be heeded because now there is no benefit in accepting after the wasiyyah has been invalidated by the qadi. The qadi can remove a wasi who is a slave, kafir, or fasiq. He said: 'Whoever appoints a slave, a kafir, or a fasiq as wasi, the qadi removes them from the wasiyyah and appoints others.' This wording indicates the validity of the wasiyyah because removal occurs after its validity. Muhammad mentioned in al-Asl that the wasiyyah is invalid. It is said: its meaning in all these cases is that the wasiyyah will become invalid. It is said: in the case of a slave, it is actually invalid due to his lack of authority and independence. In other cases it will become invalid. It is said: in the case of a kafir, it is also invalid due to his lack of authority over a Muslim. Translation: Quduri said: Whoever appoints a slave, a kafir, or a fasiq as wasi, the qadi will remove them from the wasiyyah and appoint others. Quduri's wording indicates the validity of the wasiyyah because removal occurs after validity. Muhammad mentioned in al-Mabsut that the wasiyyah is invalid. There are different interpretations. Faqih Abu al-Layth in his commentary on al-Jami' al-Saghir interpreted Muhammad's statement to mean that the wasiyyah is susceptible to being invalidated, so it is declared invalid from the start. Some said: in the case of a slave, this invalidity is literal, i.e., the wasiyyah is invalid from the beginning because the slave has no authority or independence. Some said: if a kafir is appointed, it is also invalid from the beginning because a kafir has no authority over a Muslim. The validity of the wasiyyah and the validity of the qadi's removal: 'And the basis of validity is that the capacity for supervision (al-nazar) is established for the ability of the slave in reality, and for the authority of the fasiq according to our principle, and for the authority of the kafir.'
Source pages p. 239

Commentary
This passage addresses two interrelated issues: the qadi's authority to remove a wasi (executor) and the validity of a wasiyyah when the appointed wasi is a slave, a kafir, or a fasiq. The commentator begins by explaining that if a person appointed as wasi initially refuses (by saying 'I do not accept'), the wasiyyah does not become invalid simply because of that refusal. The reason is to protect the interest of the deceased, who relied on that person. The wasi's refusal causes harm to the deceased if the wasiyyah is invalidated. However, the wasi may also suffer harm if forced to serve, but this is mitigated by the promise of reward in the Hereafter. The qadi has the authority to remove a wasi to prevent harm, and such removal is effective. After removal, the wasi cannot later accept because the wasiyyah has been nullified by the qadi's ruling. The second part discusses the case where the deceased appoints a slave, a kafir, or a fasiq as wasi. According to Quduri, the wasiyyah is valid, and the qadi may remove them and appoint someone else. Imam Muhammad holds that the wasiyyah is invalid. The commentator reconciles these views: some say it means the wasiyyah will eventually be invalidated; others say it is invalid from the start for a slave due to lack of capacity, and for a kafir due to lack of authority over a Muslim. The preferred view (as indicated by the text) is that the wasiyyah is valid, and the qadi's removal is based on his supervisory authority to ensure proper management of the deceased's estate.

Key Terms
وصی (wasi): The person appointed by the testator to execute the will and manage the estate after death.
وصیت (wasiyyah): The will or testament; the appointment of a wasi.
اخراج (ikhraj): Removal from the position of wasi by the qadi.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the preferred Hanafi view in this passage, what is the status of a wasiyyah made to a slave?
A) It is invalid from the start because a slave has no legal capacity.
B) It is valid, but the qadi may remove the slave and appoint someone else.
C) It is suspended until the slave is freed.
D) It is valid only if the master consents.

Key Takeaway
The appointment of a slave, kafir, or fasiq as wasi is valid according to the preferred Hanafi view, but the qadi may remove them to ensure proper estate management.

Wasiyyah — Bequest
intermediate
6 min
Appointment of Slave, Kafir, or Fasiq as Wasi and Qadi's Removal Power
Intra-Hanafi dispute with reconciliation via talil

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the validity of appointing a slave, kafir, or fasiq as a wasi, explain the intra-Hanafi dispute, and apply the talil (reasoning) for validity and subsequent removal.

Core Idea
Will appointing slave/kafir/fasiq is valid, but qadi must remove them due to incomplete care.

This passage addresses an important question in Hanafi wasiyyah: can a testator appoint a slave, a non-Muslim (kafir), or a sinful Muslim (fasiq) as the executor (wasi) of his will? Imam al-Quduri and Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani appear to differ, but the author of al-Hidayah reconciles their views through a careful analysis of the underlying reasoning (talil). By the end of this lesson, you will understand not only the ruling but also the legal reasoning that balances the testator's freedom with the need to protect the estate.

Guided Path
1
Identify the apparent conflict
Read Imam al-Quduri's statement and Imam Muhammad's statement in al-Asl. Note that Quduri implies validity by stating the qadi can remove the executor, while Muhammad declares the will batil. Your task is to identify the exact legal issue in dispute.
2
Examine the interpretive efforts
Several interpretations of Imam Muhammad's 'batil' are offered: some say it means 'susceptible to annulment', others say it means actually invalid for slave and kafir. Follow each interpretation and see how they reconcile with Quduri's wording.
3
Analyze the talil (reasoning) for validity
The passage provides a talil: original care (asl al-shafaqah) exists in all three because the slave is capable, the fasiq has wilayah in Hanafi usul, and the kafir has wilayah in general. Understand why this supports validity.
4
Analyze the talil for removal
The same talil explains why removal is justified: care is incomplete. For the slave, dependence on the master; for the kafir, religious enmity; for the fasiq, suspicion of betrayal. This leads to the qadi's removal power.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
Based on the commentary, the relied-upon position is that the will is valid (sahih) but the qadi may remove the executor to ensure complete care. Note the condition for the fasiq: removal only if there is fear regarding wealth.

وصیت کی صحت ، قاضی کے اخراج کی صحت کی وجہ
ووجه الصحة ثم الاخراج ان اسل النظر ثابت لقدرة العبد حقيقة وولاية الفاسق على اصلنا وولاية الكافر
في الجملة الا انه لم يتم النظر لتوقف ولاية العبد على اجازة المولى و تمكنه من الحجر بعدها والمعاداة الدينية الباعثة للكافر على ترك النظر فى حق المسلم واتهام الفاسق بالخيانة فيخرجه القاضى من الوصايا و يقيم غيره مقامه اتماماً للنظر

اور کافر میں نقصان کا باعث یہ ہے کہ وہ کافر ہے جس کو دینی دشمنی اس بات پر ابھار سکتی ہے کہ وہ مسلمان کے لئے شفقت کو چھوڑ دے۔ اور فاسق میں یہ کمی ہے کہ وہ خیانت کے ساتھ متہم ہے لہذا ان وجوہات کے پیش نظر قاضی ان کو وصایت سے خارج کر کے ان کی جگہ اور کو مقرر کر سکتا ہے تا کہ شفقت کا پورا پورا خیال رہ سکے۔
فاسق کوکب وصایت سے خارج کیا جائے گا
و شرط فى الاصل ان يكون الفاسق مخوفا عليه فى المال وهذا يصلح عذرا فی اخراجه و تبدیله بغیره ترجمہ اور مبسوط میں شرط لگائی ہے کہ فائق ایسا ہو جس پر مال کے بارے میں خوف ہو اور یہ بات ( فاسق کا ایسا ہونا جس پر مال کے بارے میں خوف ہو ) فاسق کے اخراج اور اس کی اس کے غیر کے بدلہ تبدیلی کا عذر بنے کی صلاحیت رکھتا ہے۔
And if the person whose removal is sought by the qadi says after the removal that 'I accept,' his acceptance will not be considered, because acceptance after removal has no benefit when the executorship has become invalid due to the qadi's annulment. The qadi can remove a slave, a disbeliever, or a sinner from executorship. He said: 'Whoever appoints a slave, a disbeliever, or a sinner as executor, the qadi removes them from executorship and appoints someone else.' This wording indicates the validity of the will because removal occurs after it. Muhammad mentioned in al-Asl that the will is invalid. It is said that the meaning in all these cases is that the will will become invalid. It is said that regarding a slave, the meaning is that it is actually invalid due to his lack of legal capacity and independence. For others, the meaning is that it will become invalid. It is also said that regarding a disbeliever, it is also invalid due to his lack of authority over a Muslim. Explanation: If Zaid appoints Khalid's slave, or a disbeliever, or a sinner as his executor, Imam Quduri said that the qadi will remove all three from executorship and appoint someone else. Here the author of al-Hidayah comments that Imam Quduri's statement clarifies that the will is valid, because removal occurs only after the will is valid. Imam Muhammad in al-Mabsut said that the will is invalid. Now there are different opinions regarding its explanation. Faqih Abu al-Layth in his commentary of al-Jami' al-Saghir explained the meaning of Imam Muhammad's statement as that the will in these three cases is worthy of being declared invalid, so it is called invalid beforehand. Some scholars said that regarding a slave, this invalidity is applied to its reality, i.e., the will is invalid from the start because the slave does not have authority and is not independent since he is under his master's control. And some said that if a disbeliever is appointed, it is also invalid from the start because a disbeliever has no authority over a Muslim and has no capacity to be a guardian. The reason for validity and then removal: 'The reason for validity and then removal is that the original care is established due to the slave's actual capability, and the sinner's authority according to our principle, and the disbeliever's authority in general, except that care is not complete because the slave's authority depends on the master's permission and the master's ability to place restrictions after it, and because of the religious enmity that incites the disbeliever to abandon care for the Muslim, and the sinner is suspected of betrayal. So, the qadi removes them from executorship and appoints someone else in their place to complete the care.' Explanation: Those who said that the will is valid and then the qadi's removal is also valid – here the author states the reason for validity and then the reason for removal. The summary is that for these three, the will is declared valid because they have original care, but there is deficiency in it. Due to the presence of the original, validity occurs, and due to the deficiency, removal is valid. As for how original capability exists: the slave is a sane adult, so he is capable of transactions; the sinner has authority according to our principle; and as for the disbeliever, he also has authority in general, e.g., if a disbeliever buys a Muslim slave, his purchase is valid, and the purchaser gains authority over the slave, though he is compelled to sell the Muslim slave. Anyway, this shows that the disbeliever also has authority in general, but none of them have complete and perfect care. Because the slave's authority depends on the master's consideration: if the master permits, it remains; otherwise, it ends, and even after permission, the master can restrict him. The deficiency in the disbeliever is that he is a disbeliever, and religious enmity may incite him to abandon care for the Muslim. The deficiency in the sinner is that he is suspected of betrayal. Therefore, in view of these reasons, the qadi can remove them from executorship and appoint someone else in their place to ensure complete care. A condition in al-Asl is that the sinner must be such that there is fear concerning his handling of wealth, and this serves as an excuse for his removal and replacement.
Source pages p. 240

Commentary
This passage deals with an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the validity of a will appointing a slave, a disbeliever (kafir), or a sinner (fasiq) as an executor (wasi). The text begins by presenting Imam al-Quduri's statement that the qadi can remove such persons from executorship. The author of al-Hidayah notes that this wording implies the will is valid, because removal presupposes a valid appointment. However, Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani in al-Mabsut states that such a will is invalid (batil). The commentator then explains the various interpretations: some say the will is merely susceptible to being declared invalid (so it is called invalid in anticipation), others say it is actually invalid for the slave due to lack of legal capacity, and similarly for the disbeliever due to lack of authority over a Muslim. The text then reconciles these views by providing the reasoning for validity and subsequent removal. The original care (asl al-shafaqah) exists in all three: the slave is capable in reality, the sinner has authority according to the Hanafi principle, and the disbeliever has authority in general. However, this care is not complete. The slave's authority depends on the master's permission; the disbeliever may be influenced by religious enmity; and the sinner is suspected of betrayal. Therefore, the qadi may remove them to ensure complete care. Finally, a condition is mentioned: the removal of the sinner is specifically when there is fear concerning his handling of wealth. This shows that the ruling is nuanced: the will is valid in principle, but the qadi has the power to supervise and replace the executor for valid reasons.

Key Terms
وصی (wasi): Executor appointed in a will to manage the estate after death.
ولایت (wilayah): Legal authority or capacity to act on behalf of another, here regarding management of the estate.
فاسق (fasiq): A Muslim who commits major sins or persists in minor sins, lacking moral reliability.

Key Terms from Source Passage

According to the relied-upon Hanafi position in this passage, what is the ruling on appointing a slave as a wasi?
A) The appointment is invalid from the start.
B) The appointment is valid, but the qadi may remove the slave from executorship.
C) The appointment is valid and the qadi has no power to remove the slave.
D) The appointment is valid only if the master consents.

Key Takeaway
A will appointing a slave, kafir, or fasiq is valid in Hanafi law, but the qadi may remove such executors to protect the estate due to incomplete fiduciary care.

Validity and Removal of Executors: Slave, Fasiq, and Non-Muslim
Explaining validity and removal of executors due to deficient compassion

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on appointing a slave, fasiq, or non-Muslim as executor, and explain the judge's power to remove them due to deficient compassion.

Core Idea
An executor's appointment is valid even if the person is a slave, sinner, or non-Muslim, but the judge may remove them if their compassion is deficient.

In this passage, the author of al-Hidayah addresses a nuanced fiqh issue: can a slave, a sinful person (fasiq), or a non-Muslim be appointed as an executor (wasi)? While these appointments are valid in Hanafi law, the judge retains the authority to remove them if their compassion for the beneficiaries is incomplete. This dual ruling—validity coupled with potential removal—reflects the school's concern for both legal capacity and substantive welfare.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three types of executors
The passage discusses the appointment of a slave, a fasiq (sinner), and a non-Muslim (kafir) as executor. Note that the ruling is the same for all three: the appointment is valid in principle.
2
Understand the basis for validity
Each type possesses original compassion (shafqah) and legal authority (wilayah) in some form. The slave is capable, the fasiq has authority per Hanafi principle, and the non-Muslim has authority in some respects (e.g., buying a Muslim slave).
The authority of the non-Muslim is limited but exists.
3
Recognize the deficiency that triggers removal
Their compassion is incomplete: the slave's authority depends on the master's permission; the non-Muslim's religious enmity may lead him to neglect the Muslim's interests; the fasiq is suspected of treachery. These deficiencies justify removal.
4
Note the judge's role and the condition for fasiq
The judge can remove any of them and appoint a replacement to ensure full compassion. For the fasiq, a condition from al-Mabsut is added: he is removed only if he is feared for his handling of wealth (makhufan alayhi fi al-mal).
This condition limits arbitrary removal.
